+Jamison Brereton

5 (625)
As╠Бvins
Brahm─Бtithi K─Бс╣Зva
39 verses: g─Бyatr─л, except br╠еhat─л 37тАУ38, anuс╣гс╣нubh 39, all arranged in trcas ╠е
This long hymn (at 39 verses the longest hymn to the A┼Ыvins in the R╠еgveda) presents few difficulties and, correspondingly, few particular pleasures. Many p─Бdas in the hymn have exact or near counterparts elsewhere.
The hymn begins not with the A┼Ыvins but with the appearance of the (unnamed) Dawn (vs. 1), as a lead-in to the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ early morning journey. Throughout the hymn the two gods are urged to drive here to our sacrifice, with occasional mentions of the sacrifices they should pass over on their way to ours (esp. vss. 13, 15). They are also begged for the usual assortment of wealth in goods and livestock; their тАЬrefreshmentsтАЭ (├нс╣г) are especially insistently hoped for (see vss. 5, 9, 10, 20, 21, 31, 34, 36). There is almost no mythological material, little mention of the miraculous rescues that are the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ stock in trade. Brief allusions to two of these exploits are found in verses 22тАУ23, and the bare names of a number of their clients are listed in verses 25тАУ26.
The last three verses (37тАУ39) are a d─Бnastuti praising the gift of one Ka┼Ыu, lord of the Cedis. His previous, fairly modest, gift is mentioned in verse 38, with the hope that the A┼Ыvins will have the opportunity to see a more magnificent version in verse 37. And in verse 39 Ka┼Ыu is implicitly challenged to make an unparalleled gift, so that other men will not win greater praise for their generosity.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen the shining dawn, advancing hither from afar, whitens (all things), she spreads the light on allsides.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

When, though being at a distance, she of ruddy breath has brightened as if right here,
she has stretched out her radiance in all directions.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

├б┼Ыi┼Ыvitat is an isolated verbal form; the stem is otherwise not attested. Grassmann identifies it as the тАЬAor. des Caus.,тАЭ and formally this is possible (type atitrasat тАШmade terrifiedтАЩ тИЪtras). However, there is no trans./caus *┼Ыvet├бyati to which it could have been generated, and there is no possible direct object in this passage to justify a trans./caus. reading. It is more likely a nonce intrans. redupl. aor. (type apaptat тАШflewтАЩ тИЪpat) created to substitute for the s-aor. a┼Ыvait (or the root aor. *a┼Ыvet on which a┼Ыvait is built, acdg. to Narten), which would not fit the expected iambic cadence of dimeter verse. The i root vocalism of тИЪ┼Ыvit would account for the redupl. vowel, which would by chance coincide with the redupl. vowel expected for a causative aorist: short i before the initial cluster.

+Griffith

WHEN, even as she were present here, red Dawn hath shone from far away,
She spreadeth light on every side.

+Geldner

Sobald die r├╢tlichscheinende Usas von fern her, als ob sie hier w├дre, aufschimmert, so hat sie allenthalben ihren Glanz ausgebreitet.

+Grassmann

Da sie von ferne hier erschien und hell die rothe leuchtete, so strahlte weithin sie das Licht.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAnd you, A┼Ыvins, of goodly aspect, accompany the dawn like leader with your mighty chariot harnessedat a thought.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Manfully, o wondrous ones, with your mind-yoked chariot of broad dimensions
you accompany Dawn, o A┼Ыvins.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou take nс╣Ыv├бt as standing for nс╣Ыv├бt─Б, on the basis of VI.62.10 nс╣Ыv├бt─Б r├бthena, but there seems no reason to do so, since the adverbial neut. nс╣Ыv├бt is wellattested.

+Griffith

Like Heroes on your will-yoked car farshining, Wonder-Workers! ye
Attend, O Asvins, on the Dawn.

+Geldner

Auf dem m├дnnerfahrenden, gedankengeschirrten, breitgestaltigen Wagen folget ihr Meister Asvin der Usas.

+Grassmann

Wie Helden, pr├дcht’ges Ritterpaar, auf geistgeschirrtem strahlenden Gef├дhrt begleitet Uschas ihr.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬBy you, affluent in sacrifices, may our praises be severally accepted; I bear the words (of theworshipper) like a messenger (to you).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O you rich in prizewinning mares, praise songs have appeared facing you two.
Like a messenger I shall solemnly proclaim my speech.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The Pp. analyses the sequence y├бthohiс╣гe as y├бth─Б ohiс╣гe, which would be, to say the least, unusual sandhi (though see t├бsy├йhi in VIII.3.12). Nonetheless, the context favors a connection with the root тИЪ┼лh тАШsolemnly proclaim, etc.тАЩ with pres.

├│ha- (in my opinion); cf. I.30.4 v├бcas t├бd … ohase тАЬI solemnly proclaim this speech,тАЭ with a 1st sg. -se form, as apparently also here. For this passage I assume a form ┼лhiс╣гe, built to the presential perf. ┼лh├й. This is also K├╝mmelтАЩs solution (488-89), though he assigns the form to тИЪv─Бh тАШanerkennenтАЩ, which, acdg. to him, is at least synchronically separate from тИЪoh. Renou and Lubotsky assign the form instead to тИЪvah тАШconveyтАЩ. For further disc. cf. Oldenberg and Geldner (n. 3c).

+Jamison Brereton

the A┼ЫvinsтАФfor their helpтАФ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the three compounds beginning with puru- in ab.

I emend the accented nom. k├бс╣Зv─Бsaс╕е to accentless *kaс╣Зv─Бsaс╕е, thus avoiding the awk. тАЬI shall praise (and also) the K─Бс╣Зvas (shall praise)тАЭ (so Renou), or the necessity of taking stuс╣г├й as an infinitive. Nearby VIII.7.32 has #k├бс╣Зv─Бsaс╕е … /#stuс╣г├й …, with a p─Бda-init. accented voc. k├бс╣Зv─Бsaс╕е (cf. also VIII.2.38, and with nom. VIII.4.2, VIII.6.31), and the accent here may have been acquired redactionally on these models. By my interpr. тАЬIтАЭ (the poet, who is himself a K─Бс╣Зva) announces to his fellow K─Бс╣Зvas that he is invoking the A┼Ыvins тАЬfor our helpтАЭ (na ┼лt├бye); the 1st pl.

enclitic naс╕е encompasses the poet himself and those addressed in the voc.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner and Renou I (reluctantly) supply imperative тАШgiveтАЩ in ab. It is barely possibly (but I think unlikely) that ukс╣гatam in c is a pun, belonging to тИЪukс╣г тАШsprinkleтАЩ in c, but тИЪvakс╣г/ukс╣г тАШincreaseтАЩ in ab, with the meaning тАЬincrease good wisdom for the pious man.тАЭ (Kiehnle 1979: 152 takes it to тАШincreaseтАЩ in the whole vs.) Unfortunately there are no certain exx. of the act. suffix-accented stem ukс╣г├бti to тИЪvakс╣г тАШincreaseтАЩ (though see med. part. ukс╣г├бm─Бс╣Зa- and isolated root-accented part. ├║kс╣гant-), and even if so, we would probably expect them to be intrans., at least on the basis of pf.

vav├бkс╣гa, etc., and the just cited pres. forms.

The hapax ├бvit─Бriс╣З─л- is clearly derived from v├н тИЪtс╣Э, but its meaning is variously rendered. Grassmann (S─Бyaс╣Зa) тАШenduring, lastingтАЩ, Geldner тАЬdie nicht auf sich warten l├дsstтАЭ (doesnтАЩt keep (s.o.) waiting), on the basis of X.34.6. However, I take that passage in the Gambler hymn to mean тАШrun counterтАЩ (adopting the tr. of Macdonell), or more pointedly тАШdoublecrossтАЩ, the tr. I use here, though something like тАШthwartтАЩ would convey the sense of this idiom as well.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWith which in three days and three nights you traverse from afar all the brilliant (constellations).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

With which you fly around the three far distances, all the luminous realms of heaven,
and the three nights.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The acc. phrases tisr├бс╕е par─Бv├бtaс╕е, div├│ v├н┼Ыv─Бni rocan─Б╠Б, and tr─л╠Бm╠Рr akt┼л╠Бn are all accusatives of extent and presented as if they were parallel; the specification тАШthreeтАЩ in the first and last underlines this supposed parallelism. But the first two express extent of space and the third extent of time. A better tr. might be тАЬyou fly around the three far distances (and? see below) all the luminous realms of heaven for or during three nights. I do not know what тАЬthree nightsтАЭ refers to: there is no parallel locution elsewhere and the standard tr. do not comment. It may simply reflect the common association of the A┼Ыvins with triplets of various sorts. See esp.

I.34, which does have a roughly similar expression: I.34.7 tr├нс╕е тАж div├й-dive тАЬThree times, day after day тАжтАЭ As for the first two accusative phrases, the rocan─Б╠Б(ni) are regularly qualified as тАШthreeтАЩ, so тАЬall the luminous realmsтАЭ may be synonymous with immediately preceding тАЬthe three far distancesтАЭ (a phrase also found in I.34.7 and VIII.32.22).

+Griffith

Wherewith the three wide distances, and all the lights that are in heaven.
Ye traverse, and three times of night.

+Geldner

Mit denen ihr die drei Entfernungen, alle Lichter des Himmels, die drei Nachtzeiten durchflieget.

+Grassmann

Mit denen die drei Fernen ihr und alles, was am Himmel gl├дnzt, Drei dunkle R├дume ihr durchfliegt.

+Elizarenkova

рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╣рд░реНрд╡рд┐рджрд╛ рдЕрд╣реНрдиреЛ рд▓рдореНрднрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░реМ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрд╣реНрдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рддрд╕рдордпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпреМ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╡реНрдпреМ ред рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рдЧреЛрдорддреАрдГ рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рд░реНрдЧреЛрдВрднрд┐рд░реНрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ рдЗрд╖рдГ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рджрддреНрддрдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╕рд╛рддреАрдГ рд╕рдВрднрдЬрдиреАрдпрд╛ рджрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд░рд╛рдпрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рджрддреНрддрдореН ред рд╕рдирддреЗрдГ рд╕рдиреЛрддреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдХреНрддрд┐рдиреН ред тАШрдЬрдирд╕рдирдЦрдирд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рддреНрд╡рдореН ред’ рдЙрддрд┐рдпреВрддрд┐’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдХреНрддрд┐рди рдЙрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдВ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪрд╛рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рд╛рддрдпреЗ рдЙрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧрд╡рд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рд▓рд╛рднрд╛рдп рд╕рдВрднрдЬрдирд╛рдп рд╡рд╛ рдкрдердГ рддрджреБрдкрд╛рдпрд░реВрдкрд╛рдиреН рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐ рд╕рд┐рддрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рдмрдзреНрдиреАрддрдореН ред рдпрдерд╛рдиреНрдпреЗ рди рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╢рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдХреБрд░реБрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред ‘рд╖рд┐рдЮреН рдмрдиреНрдзрдиреЗ ред рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реЛ рд╡рд┐рдХрд░рдгрд╕реНрдп рд▓реБрдХреН ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЙрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╡рд╢рд╛рджрдпрдВ рдзрд╛рддреБрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд┐рдкрд░реАрддреЗ рдмрдиреНрдзрдирд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдорд░рдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдорд┐рддрд┐ рдпрдерд╛ред рдкрдереЛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐ рд╕рд┐рддрдВ рд╡рд┐рдореБрдЮреНрдЪрддрдореН ред рдкреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рдпрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдкрдерд┐рдЮреНрдЫрдмреНрджреЛрд╜рдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдп рд╢рд╕рд┐ рдЯрд┐рд▓реЛрдк рдЙрджрд╛рддреНрддрдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░реЗрдг рд╢рд╕ рдЙрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬBringers of the day, (bestow) upon us food with cattle, or donations of wealth, and close the path(against aggression) upon our gains.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

And close the path: vi pathaс╕е s─Бtaye sitam = asm─Бkam gav─Бd─лn─Бml─Бbh─Бya tadup─Бyar┼лp─Бn m─Бrg─Бn vi┼Ыeс╣гeс╣Зa badhn─лtam yath─Бnye na pravi┼Ыanti;

Vi = vimu├▒catampradar┼Ыayatam ma-rg─Бn, open, or, show to us the paths of profit

+Jamison Brereton

And refreshments along with cattle and winnings, too, o finders of the daysтАФ
unfasten the paths for us to win (them).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Renou (explicitly) and Geldner (implicitly) supply as the verb of ab voс╕╖h├бm тАШconveyтАЩ from 10c. This is not impossible, and the duplication of some vocabulary (9a g├│mat─лr ├нс╣гa(с╕е): 10 g├│mantam тАж ray├нm тАж ├б┼Ыv─Бvatir ├нс╣гaс╕е) may favor it. But the two verses belong to different tс╣Ыcas, a fact that should disfavor such automatic filling in the blanks. I in fact think that ab can be construed with c. That p─Бda asks the gods to тАЬunfastenтАЭ the paths (v├н path├бс╕е тАж sitam), in other words, to make the way clear, for winning (s─Бt├бye). The dat. infinitive s─Бt├бye frequently takes an accusative of what is to be won (among many exx., cf., e.g., IX.88.2 pur┼л╠Бс╣Зi s─Бt├бye v├бs┼лni). I see no reason why the accusatives of ab cannot be the object of this infinitive; with the acc. in b, s─Бt─л╠Бс╕е, we would have not only a cognate accusative construction, but one involving two forms of the same stem. Alternatively the accusatives in ab could serve as objects of v├н тАж sitam, thus parallel to path├бс╕е. Cf. VIII.23.29, where both accusatives found here are the objects of ├бp─Б vс╣Ыdhi тАШuncoverтАЩ, semantically similar to v├н тАж sitam: VIII.23.29bc tv├бс╣Г no g├│mat─лr ├нс╣гaс╕е / mah├│ r─Бy├бс╕е s─Бt├нm agne ├бp─Б vс╣Ыdhi тАЬUncover for us refreshments consisting of cows and the winning of great wealth, o Agni.тАЭ Hence in our passage тАЬ(Unfasten) refreshments and winnings; unfasten the paths for winning.тАЭ See further disc. ad vs. 21 below, which lends additional support to the 2nd alternative.

The epithet aharv├нd- (4x, twice in this hymn) can contain either тИЪvid тАШknowтАЩ or тИЪvid тАШfindтАЩ. Geldner (and Grassmann) opt for the former, with Geldner generalizing it to тАШZeitkennerтАЩ.

Scarlatta (480-81) considers either possible, though his tr. reflect the former. In I.2.2 and I.156.4 I choose тАШknowтАЩ, because both passages seem to involve knowledge of the ritual day, but esp. in the latter I recognize the possibility of тАШfindтАЩ. (See comm. thereon.) By contrast the published translation of this hymn has тАШfindтАЩ for both occurrences. I do not feel strongly either way, but since this hymn begins with the A┼Ыvins accompanying Dawn (vss. 1-2) and the immediately preceding vs. (8) has a mention of their traversing the nights, I mildly favor тАШfindтАЩ, expressing the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ advent in the early morning, bringing the daylight with them. Note also svarvid─Б тАШfinders of the sunтАЩ of the A┼Ыvins in nearby VIII.8.7. This latter well-attested cmpd. seems universally to be analysed as containing тАШfindтАЩ, not тАШknowтАЩ; cf. Scarlatta 491-92.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAffluent i sacrifices, grant to us who are opulent (in oblations) a spacious unassailable dwelling.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O you rich in prizewinning mares, to us and to our bounteous (patrons) hold out extensive
shelter that cannot be cheated.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. v─Бjin─лvas┼л recurs here from 3a; in both verses it is immediately preceded by a heavy dat. pronoun, the near-rhyming yuv─Б╠Бbhy─Бm and asm├бbhyam. Its other two occurrences in this hymn (vss. 19, 30) are not so structured.

тАЬShelter that cannot be cheated (/deceived)тАЭ (see also VIII.85.5) is a striking and somewhat opaque expression, since ├бd─Бbhya- usually modifies animate beings (generally gods) who arenтАЩt gullible. I assume that the intention is shelter that canтАЩt be breached by trickery, vel sim., but the context of neither passage gives us any help.

+Griffith

Wide shelter, ne’er to be assailed.

Gew├дhret uns, ihr Gewinnreichen, und unseren G├╢nnern in ganzer Breite euren untr├╝glichen Schirm!

+Grassmann

Uns und den Opferherrn verleiht, o g├╝terreiche, euren Schutz, Den weiten, unverletzlichen.

+Wilson
English translation:

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who ever carefully: brahma jan─Бn─Бm y─Бviс╣гс╣нam t┼лyam─Б gatam: br─Бhmaс╣Зa j─Бtim, thebr─Бhmaс╣Зa class; or, parivс╣Ыdham stotram havirlakс╣гaс╣Зam annam v─Б, the great praise or sacrificial food

+Jamison Brereton

Team up the formulations of the people and come quickly here.
Do not go to the others.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The Pp. analyses y─Б╠Бviс╣гс╣нam as y─Б╠Б├бviс╣гс╣нam, with the latter an injunc. -iс╣г-aor.

to тИЪav тАШhelp, favorтАЩ. Geldner accepts this analysis and Renou is sympathetic; however, Oldenberg dismisses it, taking y─Б╠Бviс╣гс╣нam rather to тИЪyu тАШuniteтАЩ, as the verbal counterpart (with initial preverb n├н) of the common noun niy├║t- тАШteamтАЩ. This analysis is already found in Grassmann and is vigorously defended by Narten (Sig. Aor. 212). One argument against the Pp. interpr. is the fact that this would produce an unambiguous embedded relative clause, and these are rare to non-existent in the RV.

English translation:

+Jamison Brereton

You, o A┼ЫvinsтАФdrink of this dear exhilarating drink,
of the honey bestowed, o holy ones.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The partitive gen. with pibatam consists of the phrase asy├б тАж m├бdasya c─Б╠Бruс╣Зaс╕е / m├бdhvo r─Бt├бsya, rendered in the published translation (sim. Geldner) as тАЬ of тАЬthis dear exhilarating drink, of the honey bestowed,тАЭ which faithfully represents the hemistich boundary. However, it also construes the adj. c─Б╠Бruс╣Зaс╕е with masc. m├бdasya, though u-stem sg. oblique forms with interposed -n- should of course only be neut. This is in fact the only certain ex. of such a masc. form given by Lanman (Noun inflec., 410).

There are several ways to avoid this undesirable morphological analysis. The least attractive is to take m├бda- here as adjectival, but this exceptionally well-attested stem is otherwise only a noun. The other two possibilities are better. On the one hand, the rest of the gen. phrase includes the neut. noun m├бdhvaс╕е, and c─Б╠Бruс╣Зaс╕е can be construed with it: тАЬof this exhilarating drink, of the dear honey тАжтАЭ The drawback is that this artificially splits the gen. in b and reads part of it across the hemistich boundary. Perhaps the best solution is suggested by the other four occurrences of c─Б╠Бruс╣Зaс╕е, which always modifies amс╣Ы╠Бtasya тАШ(drink) of immortalityтАЩ, with the nominalized amс╣Ы╠Бta- neuter (IV.70.2, 4; 108.4; 100.4, always in the order amс╣Ы╠Бtasya c─Б╠Бruс╣Зaс╕е, p─Бda-final as here). I suggest we read c─Б╠Бruс╣Зaс╕е here as representing that phrase and tr. тАЬof this exhilarating drink, of the dear (drink of immorality), of the honey тАжтАЭ

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬBringers of the day, you rain upon us by the (open) door (of the clouds) the waters of heaven, or (withthem fill) the rivers.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

And heavenly refreshments and rivers, o finders of the daysтАФ like two doors, you will open (these) up for us.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is structured very like vs. 9, presenting some of the same syntactic problems, but in a somewhat clearer fashion. The first two p─Бdas, ut├б no divy─Б╠Б├нс╣гa, ut├б s├нndh┼лm╠Рr aharvid─Б are identical to 9ab ut├б no g├│mat─лr ├нс╣гa, ut├б s─Бt─л╠Бr aharvid─Б, save for the adj. modifying ├нс╣гaс╕е in a and the acc. pl. found in b. Recall that Geldner and Renou supply a verb (voс╕╖h├бm) for ab, separating those p─Бdas from c. Some support for their position might be found in the larger context of vs. 21: the immediately preceding p─Бda, 20c, contains v├бhatam with a variant ├нс╣гaс╕е object (тАЬfat,тАЭ not тАЬheavenlyтАЭ). So it could be possible to read 21ab as a continuation of the VP in 20c, giving support to Geldner/Renou, who supply a verb from the same root (тИЪvah) to govern the identically structured 9ab. But Geldner happily takes ab as the obj. of the verb in 21c, ├бpa тАж varс╣гathaс╕е тАШyou two will open upтАЩ (s-aor. subjunctive to тИЪvс╣Ы тАШcover, obstructтАЩ). As was noted ad vs. 9, ├бpa тИЪvс╣Ы тАШuncover, open upтАЩ is semantically very like v├н тИЪs─Б тАШunfastenтАЩ, and if refreshments can be the object of the first, this should also be possible for the second.

varс╣гathaс╕е is the only s-aor. form to тИЪvс╣Ы in all of Sanskrit. It is very possible that it was created for this passage because the resulting syllable varс╣г evokes the root тИЪvс╣Ыс╣г тАШrainтАЩ, which would be appropriate for the liquids that are its objects in ab. Renou also remarks on this word play.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen did the son of Tugra, thrown into the ocean, glorify you, leaders (of rites)? then when yourchariot and horses descended.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

When did the son of Tugra, abandoned in the sea, do reverence to you, o men,
so that your chariot would fly with its birds?

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The subjunctive p├бt─Бt seems to be used in an unusual past prospective sense in this mythological context. This may be an English problem, however. Since the verb of the main clause is injunc. vidhat, this context is not necessarily preterital, but тАЬtimeless,тАЭ and the subjunctive can therefore be expressing pure future modality.

The fact that the next verse is also mythological and contains an undoubted present tense form da┼Ыasyathaс╕е shows that mythological tense is fluid here. Renou remarks (ad vs. 23) that the indifference between present and preterite underlines the reflection of the current human situation in the legendary material.

+Griffith

When did the son of’ Tugra serve you, Men? Abandoned in the sea,
That with winged steeds your car might fly.

+Geldner

+Grassmann

Wann rief des Tugra Sohn euch an, ins Meer gest├╝rzt, o M├дnner, dass Eur Wagen fl├╢ge rossbespannt.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

su┼Ыast├нbhiс╕е in p─Бda b is taken by Geldner (also Grassmann) as modifying ┼лt├нbhiс╕е in p─Бda a (тАЬmit diesen l├╢blichen HilfenтАЭ; Geldner takes n├бvyas─лbhiс╕е as adverbial тАЬaufs neueтАЭ), but this requires su┼Ыast├н- to be adjectival. However, almost all occurrences of this stem – and all seven other instr. – are nouns (тАШgood laudтАЩ)(and see nominal suс╣гс╣нut├нm тАШgood praiseтАЩ, identically formed and nearly synonymous, in 30c below). Although in G─Бyatr─л the b-p─Бda more regularly construes with the a-p─Бda, it is not out of the question for it to go with c instead. In this case the instr. phrase of b goes well with c, and it would only represent one constituent fronted before the subordinating y├бd.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs., like the almost identical IV.46.4, is syntactically somewhat ragged: the beginning of p─Бda c, ─Б╠Бh├н sth─Б╠Бthaс╕е, should ideally be the beginning of the clause, given the fronted preverb and the h├н. But the object occupies all of ab (and the end of c).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntactic disorder continues here. The main clause corresponding to vs. 28 is vs. 30; this intermediate verse, the middle one of the tс╣Ыca, is an elaborate nominal sentence couched entirely in the nominative and functions as an extensive parenthesis further specifying the features of the chariot found in 28a (in the acc.).

On ubh─Б╠Бcakr─Б╠БтАЬboth wheels,тАЭ with apparent neut. pl. for expected du cakr├й see comm. ad X.10.8.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬImmortal A┼Ыvins, destroyers of the cities of the D─Бsas, you bring to us food from afar.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

P┼лrv─лra┼Ыnantau d─Бs─лс╕е: pur─лс╕е or bahv─лс╕е, many; so, taking away much food from the enemy, you bring it to us

+Jamison Brereton

From far away you convey here the many refreshments
of the D─Бsa, while consuming them, o immortal A┼Ыvins.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The sense of this vs. is a little odd: it sounds as if the A┼Ыvins on their journey are snacking on the comestibles they are bringing to us and we will only get the scraps. This is not the usual way to urge the gods to bring us things and makes the A┼Ыvins sound mingy. Perhaps the point is rather that there are so many (p┼лrv─л╠Бс╕е) refreshments that thereтАЩs enough for everyone? Geldner compares 19c, which does not seem similar to me.

+Griffith

From far away ye come to us, Asvins, enjoying plenteous food
Of Dasas, O Immortal Ones.

+Geldner

Ihr bringet aus der Ferne die vielen dem Dasa geh├╢renden guten Speisen mit, sie verzehrend, ihr unsterblichen Asvin.

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

+Jamison Brereton

Let your feathered birds [=horses], frothing at the mouth, convey you here to the man who performs the ceremony well.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation тАЬfeathered birds, frothing at the mouthтАЭ is, to say the least, inelegant and perhaps unintelligible. What I think is meant: the birds are compared to horses (or the horses to birds); pruс╣гit├бpsavaс╕е тАШfrothing at the mouthтАЩ qualifies the underlying horses and indicates their speed. Cf. the overt horses in V.75.6 ├б┼Ыv─Бsaс╕е pruс╣гit├бpsavaс╕е, VIII.87.5 ├б┼Ыvebhiс╕е pruс╣гit├бpsubhiс╕е (both A┼Ыvin hymns)(latter =VIII.13.11 [Indra]).

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬNo hostile force arrests that car of yours which is hymned (by the devout), and which is laden with food.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Your chariot pursuing our songтАФthe (chariot) that rolls along, along with its refreshmentтАФ
its wheel does not ram against it.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax -g─Бyas- (a hapax) in ├бnug─Бyasam- is generally taken as a primary s-stem to the diphthongal root тИЪg─Б i╠п ; see Whitney (Roots), AiG II.2.235, EWA s.v. тИЪG─А2 . The contextual question is what is following what. For Geldner the song is sounding after/following the chariot (тАЬGesang schallt eurem Wagen nachтАЭ), but most ├бnu- compounds have the structure тАЬfollowing X,тАЭ where X is the 2nd member (e.g., ├бnu-patha- тАШfollowing/along the pathтАЩ; with diff. accent anu-k─Бm├б- тАШfollowing/according to desireтАЩ). I therefore think the chariot is following the song; in other words, it is making its way to the ritual ground, drawn to the song being sung there. Rather like the modern expression тАЬfollow the money.тАЭ P─Бda b seems to be a clear embedded relative clause – or else, at least as I have punctuated it, a parenthesis.

The point of c seems to be that the wheel doesnтАЩt knock against the chariot no matter how fast it moves. Such knocking presumably would be a problem with wheels that were not securely fastened to their axle and well balanced, so the A┼ЫvinтАЩs chariot is, not surprisingly, well constructed.

+Griffith

The whcel delayeth not that car of yours accompanied by song,
That cometh with a store of food.

+Geldner

Gesang schallt eurem Wagen nach, der mit guter Speise kommt; ihn st├╢├Яt das Rad nicht.

+Grassmann

Und euer Wagen, liedumt├╢nt, der rollt, mit Nahrung angef├╝llt, Wird nicht gehemmt von seinem Rad.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAffluent in showers, taste the wakeful desirable Soma; combine for us riches with food.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You sweeten, as it were, the wakeful wild animal [=soma?], o you of bullish goods.
Infuse wealth with refreshment for us.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

With S─Бyaс╣Зa I take the wakeful wild beast to be soma. The obj. of тИЪsvad is regularly an oblation, and in IX.105.1 its object, soma, is compared to a ┼Ы├н┼Ыu-, the young of an animal or human.

v─Б in b cannot be the disjunctive тАШorтАЩ, as there is no disjunction possible. I take it as the short form of iva тАШlikeтАЩ (with lengthening), as Geldner also seems to (on the grounds of his тАЬsozusagenтАЭ), marking the statement as an approximative. OldenbergтАЩs comment is not entirely intelligible, but he seems rather to imply that v─Б expresses a strong positive, and I therefore assume he thinks itтАЩs a form of va├н, as do Renou and Klein (DGRV II.201-2).

+Griffith

O Wealthy Gods, ye taste and find the brisk and watchful wild beast good.
Associate wealth with food for us.

+Geldner

Ihr macht das fr├╝hwache Tier sozusagen schmackhaft, ihr Sch├дtzereichen. F├╝llet unseren Besitz mit guter Speise auf!

+Grassmann

Ihr habet gern das muntre Wild, das ihr, o kr├дftige, erjagt; Erf├╝llt mit Labung unsern Schatz.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe son of Cedi, who has given me for servants ten R─Бj─Бs, bright as gold, for all men are beneath hisfeet; all those around him wear cuirasses of leather.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Give me for servants: having taken these r─Бj─Бs prisonersin battle, he gives them to me in servitude: yuddhe par─Бjit─Бn gс╣Ыhitv─Б t─Бn da- satven─Бsmai dattav─Бn; wearcuirasses of leather: carmamn─Бс╕е = carma mayasya kavav─Бder dh─Бraс╣Зe kс╣Ыt─Бbhy─Бsaс╕е, practised in wearingarmour of leader; or carma = caraс╣Зa s─Бdhan─Бni a┼Ыv─Бd─лni v─Бhan─Бni, means of going, vehicles, horses andthe like, i.e. exercised in their management in war.

+Jamison Brereton

He who (previously) bestowed on me a kingтАЩs ten (horses?) of golden appearanceтАФ
beneath the feet of the lord of the Cedis are (all) the communities, the тАЬhide-tanningтАЭ men all around.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

There is much disagreement on what to supply with h├нraс╣Зyasaс╣Гdс╣Ы┼Ыaс╕е and indeed on whether it modifies r─Б╠Бj├▒aс╕е, interpreted as an acc. pl. (see Geldner n. 38ab).

Since it seems unlikely that Ka┼Ыu gave the poet ten golden kings, even as figurines (pace Oldenberg), it seems best to take r─Б╠Бj├▒aс╕е as gen. sg. and supply another desirable golden item. Geldner suggests garments, probably in part because of the hide-tanners? Hoffmann (Inj. 229 n. 227) points out that gold(-bedecked) horses are mentioned elsewhere in d─Бnastutis, and I follow him in the published translation However, given how prominently gold figures in the description of chariots in this hymn (vss. 28-29, 35; cf. also 11), тАШchariotsтАЩ might be a better choice.

The apparently contemptuous тАШhide-tanningтАЩ (carmamn─Б╠Бс╕е) must be a way of indicating that, in comparison with Ka┼Ыu, all men hereabouts are no better than tanners: ignoble, low, and engaged in dirty and polluting activity. But perhaps thereтАЩs just a whiff of a suggestion that Ka┼Ыu has enough cows to furnish work for many tanners – and therefore he should be more generous with these cows to his poet.

+Griffith

He who hath given me for mine own ten Kings like gold to look upon.
At Caidya’s feet are all the people round about, all those who think upon the shield.

+Geldner

Der mir zehn wie Gold aussehende Kleider des K├╢nigs schenkte. Die V├╢lker reichen dem Cedisohn nicht an die F├╝├Яe; Lohgerber sind die Leute ringsum.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬNo one proceeds by that path which the Cedis follow, no other proud man as a more liberal benefactorconfers (favour on those who praise him).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let no one go by this path by which these Cedis go,

The following hymn initiates the second group of hymns in VIII, those in which the seer Vatsa is mentioned (VIII.6тАУ11); see Oldenberg (1888: 211тАУ14).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Like many d─Бnastutis, this one seems to have a bit of sting in its praise.

The poet seems at first to be saying that the Cedis are so lavish in their giving that no one else could follow them, but the 2nd half of the verse warns that all it would take for another man to receive more praise than Ka┼Ыu is to give more. Although the m─Б╠Б prohibitive of ab is technically applied to other men (тАЬlet no one go тАжтАЭ), itтАЩs really an implicit challenge to Ka┼Ыu: he can only stop others from going on his path by always giving the most.

+Griffith

No man, not any, goes upon the path on which the Cedis walk.
No other prince, no folk is held more liberal of gifts than they.

+Geldner

Keiner soll auf dem Pfade wandeln, auf dem diese Cedi┬┤s wandeln, damit nicht ein anderer Lohnherr sich r├╝hmen darf, ein noch freigebigerer Mann zu sein.

+Elizarenkova
